## USER 🧑‍💻

**Tool Response**:
```json
{
  "name": "read_file",
  "response": {
    "output": "# Anti-Patterns & Lessons Learned\n\nThis file documents approaches that failed, caused bugs, or were deprecated in favor of better patterns. Reference this before implementing new logic.\n\n## 1. Variable Initialization Dependency (ReferenceError)\n\n### The Problem\nDeclaring a `useMemo` or `useEffect` hook that references a state variable *before* the state variable itself is defined.\n\n**❌ BAD (Causes `ReferenceError`):**\n```jsx\nconst selectedData = useMemo(() => {\n  return allData.filter(item => formData.ids.includes(item.id));\n}, [allData, formData.ids]); // formData is used here...\n\nconst [formData, setFormData] = useState({ ids: [] }); // ...but defined here.\n```\n\n### The Fix\nAlways declare state hooks (`useState`) at the very top of the component, before any derivative hooks (`useMemo`, `useCallback`) or side-effect hooks (`useEffect`).\n\n**✅ GOOD:**\n```jsx\nconst [formData, setFormData] = useState({ ids: [] });\n\nconst selectedData = useMemo(() => {\n  return allData.filter(item => formData.ids.includes(item.id));\n}, [allData, formData.ids]);\n```\n\n> **Rationale:** JavaScript `const` declarations are not hoisted. `useMemo` executes its function during the initial render phase; if the dependency variable hasn't been initialized yet, the engine throws a `ReferenceError`.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Hardcoded UI Options for Centralized Entities\n\n### The Problem\nUsing hardcoded arrays for selection options (e.g., Branches, Courses, Departments) instead of fetching them from the API.\n\n**❌ BAD:**\n```jsx\n<SelectInput \n  options={[\n    { label: 'Downtown', value: 'Downtown' },\n    { label: 'West Side', value: 'West Side' }\n  ]}\n/>\n```\n\n### The Fix\nUse React Query hooks to fetch live data and map it to the selection format.\n\n**✅ GOOD:**\n```jsx\nconst { data: branches } = useBranchesQuery();\nconst options = branches?.map(b => ({ label: b.name, value: b.id })) || [];\n\n<SelectInput options={options} isLoading={!branches} />\n```\n\n> **Rationale:** Hardcoding options causes \"Source of Truth\" drift. If a branch name changes in the database, the UI remains outdated and submissions will fail validation.\n\n---\n\n## 3. UI-Centric Schema Names\n\n### The Problem\nUsing semantic names in the UI state that don't match the database schema (e.g., `dob` vs `date_of_birth`).\n\n**❌ BAD:**\n```jsx\nconst [formData, setFormData] = useState({ dob: '' });\n// Requires manual mapping before API call\nconst payload = { date_of_birth: formData.dob };\n```\n\n### The Fix\nUI state names **MUST** perfectly mirror the database entity field names.\n\n**✅ GOOD:**\n```jsx\nconst [formData, setFormData] = useState({ date_of_birth: '' });\n// Payload can be sent directly\napi.submit(formData);\n```\n\n> **Rationale:** Reduces boilerplate mapping code and prevents \"hydration mismatch\" where fetched data fails to populate the form because the field names don't match.\n"
  },
  "id": "synth_ce6dd6a1-dc77-4844-a6dd-95bd3f7c12ba_1779194171238_4"
}
```

```json
{
  "name": "read_file",
  "response": {
    "output": "# V2 Architecture & Design Patterns\n\nThe Dazzling ERP system has migrated to a **V2 Architecture** designed for high modularity, schema-driven data flows, and strict UI consistency.\n\n## 1. Core Structural Pattern: Feature-Based Modularity\n\nThe project follows a \"Feature Slice\" inspired pattern located in `src/features/`. Each domain (e.g., `batch`, `course`, `teacher`, `student`) is self-contained.\n\n### Feature Directory Structure\n```\nsrc/features/[domain]/\n├── api/             # Data fetching logic (mock & real)\n├── components/      # Feature-specific UI\n│   ├── profile/     # Deep-dive dashboard components\n│   └── forms/       # Creation/Edit forms\n├── hooks/           # TanStack Query wrappers\n├── utils/           # Mappers and domain-specific logic\n└── constants/       # Feature-specific constants\n```\n\n## 2. The Data Flow Chain\n\nBusiness logic is decoupled from UI via custom hooks, and data definitions are decoupled from implementations via a registry.\n\n**The Chain**: `UI Component` → `Query Hook` (use*Queries.js) → `api.js` → `apiClient.executeAction` → `API_REGISTRY`.\n\n### API Registry & Client\n- **`apiClient.js`**: A centralized engine that wraps all requests in a unified envelope, manages error mapping, and enforces security headers.\n- **`API_REGISTRY.js`**: A lookup table mapping frontend semantic paths to backend action strings. This allows the backend to change its endpoint structure without breaking the frontend.\n\n## 3. State Management & Initialization\n\n- **Server State**: Primary state management is handled by **TanStack Query**.\n- **Hydration Guard**: The `HydrationGuard` and `useErpHydration` hook ensure that critical data (Courses, Teachers, Batches, Branches) is pre-cached before the main UI renders, preventing \"flash of empty content.\"\n\n## 4. UI Strategy: Atomic & Compound Components\n\n- **Atomic Primitives**: Found in `src/components/ui/v2/` (e.g., `BaseInput`, `Button`).\n- **Compound Components**: Structural components like `FormField` and `FormSection` provide consistency (labels, error states, layout) across all forms.\n- **Semantic UI**: Prefer semantic wrapper components over raw HTML elements to reduce DOM depth and improve maintainability.\n\n## 5. React Query \"Cache-First\" Strategy\n\nA \"Cache-First\" data retrieval strategy is implemented for detail and edit views to reduce unnecessary server requests.\n\n### Local Relation Resolver Pattern\nWhen navigating from a list to a detail view:\n1.  **Tier 1**: Check the specific detail cache (e.g., `queryKeys.batch.detail(id)`).\n2.  **Tier 2**: Search across all cached list data (e.g., `queryKeys.batch.lists()`).\n3.  **Tier 3**: Fallback to server fetch only if Tier 1 & 2 are empty.\n\n> **Rationale**: This provides an instantaneous UI experience and significantly reduces API token usage.\n\n## 6. Dynamic Form Orchestration\n\nModern forms in the ERP (e.g., `AddTeacher.jsx`) have moved from static hardcoded arrays to **Live API Resolution**.\n\n### Key Rules for Dynamic Forms:\n- **Zero Static Options**: Selection options for Branches, Courses, and Groups **MUST** be fetched via React Query hooks (e.g., `useBranchesQuery`).\n- **Loading & Disabled States**: Form inputs dependent on external data **MUST** implement `isLoading` indicators and be `disabled` until data is ready.\n- **Mapping Strategy**: Data from the API should be mapped to the UI components' `options` format (label/value) directly within the component or via a dedicated selector hook.\n\n## 7. Schema-UI Synchronization (The Source of Truth)\n\nAll UI field names and data payloads **MUST** align perfectly with the backend `full_schema.json`.\n\n### Standards:\n- **Field Naming**: Replace legacy UI-centric names with database-accurate names (e.g., `course_name` -> `name` in Course model).\n- **ID-Based Selection**: Forms should store and transmit unique identifiers (e.g., `course_id`) rather than semantic strings (names) to maintain database integrity.\n- **Derived Labels**: Use `useMemo` hooks to resolve display names/labels from IDs for UI rendering (e.g., finding the `name` of a selected `course_id` from the cached `coursesData`).\n\n## 8. Development Workflow: Schema-Driven\n\n- **Source of Truth**: `src/Schema/full_schema.json` defines all data structures.\n- **Mocking Engine**: Every feature has a `.mockApi.js` that simulates database interactions based on the `full_schema`, allowing for rapid prototyping and offline development.\n"
  },
  "id": "synth_ce6dd6a1-dc77-4844-a6dd-95bd3f7c12ba_1779194175422_5"
}
```

---

## MODEL ✨

I have read and analyzed the project's memory files in `.gemini/memory`, including the architecture guidelines, anti-patterns, and the memory index. My internal context is now updated with the following core principles of the Dazzling ERP system:

1.  **V2 Architecture**: Feature-based modularity (located in `src/features/`), strict separation of concerns, and a centralized `API_REGISTRY` for data fetching.
2.  **State Management**: Heavy reliance on **TanStack Query** with a "Cache-First" strategy (local relation resolver) to optimize performance.
3.  **Form Standards**: UI field names must perfectly mirror the database schema (as defined in `full_schema.json`). Forms must avoid hardcoded options, instead fetching dynamic data via React Query.
4.  **Security & Integrity**: ID-based selection is preferred over semantic names, and a `HydrationGuard` ensures critical data is cached before rendering.

I am now standing by for your next instruction.

      joining_date: formData.joining_date,\n        status: formData.status,\n        subjects: formData.subjects,\n        userData: formData.createLogin ? {\n          username: formData.username || formData.salary_type.toLowerCase(),\n          base_amount: parseFloat(formData.base_salary) || 0,\n          effective_from: formData.joining_date\n        },\n        documents: formData.profile_photo_url ? [\n          {\n            document_type: \"id_proof\", \n            file_url: formData.profile_photo_url\n          }\n        ] : []\n      };\n\n      addMutation.mutate(requestPayload, {\n errorsMap[item.field] = item.message;\n              });\n              setFieldErrors(errorsMap);\n              setError(err.message || 'Please fix the errors highlighted below.');\n            } isFetchingTeacher) {\n    return (\n      <div className=\"flex items-center justify-center min-h-[400px]\">\n        <div className=\"size-12 border-4 border-primary/30 border-t-primary rounded-full animate-spin\"></div>\n      </div>\n    );\n  }\n\n  return (\n    <div className=\"pb-32\">\n      <CourseSelectionModal \n        isOpen={isCourseModalOpen}\n        onClose={() => '100%' : '25%'}</span>\n        </div>\n      </header>\n\n      {error && (\n        <div className=\"mx-4 lg:mx-0 mb-6 bg-red-50 dark:bg-red-900/20 text-red-600 p-4 rounded-lg border border-red-100 dark:border-red-800 flex items-center gap-3 animate-in fade-in slide-in-from-top-2\">\n          <span className=\"material-symbols-outlined\">error</span>\n          <span className=\"text-sm font-bold\">{error}</span>\n        </div>\n      )}\n\n      <form className=\"space-y-6 px-4 lg:px-0\" onSubmit={handleSubmit}>\n        {/* Section 1 & 2: Grid Layout */}\n        <div className=\"grid grid-cols-1 lg:grid-cols-2 gap-6\">\n          {/* 1. ---

## MODEL ✨

The `AddTeacher.jsx` page handles the save button success response through a structured `onSuccess` callback within the `handleSubmit` function. It distinguishes between **Edit Mode** (Update) and **New Registration** (Create).

### 1. Analysis of the Success Handler

The logic is split into two branches depending on the `isEditMode` flag:

#### **A. Edit Mode (Update Mutation)**
When updating an existing teacher, the success response is handled as follows:
```javascript
updateMutation.mutate({ id, data: profileData }, {
  onSuccess: (res) => {
    if (res.success) {
      // Redirects to the specific teacher's profile page
      navigate(`/admin/teachers/${id}`);
    } else {
      // If res.success is false, it sets a general error message
      setError(res.message || 'Failed to update profile.');
    }
  },
  onError: (err) => setError(err.message)
});
```

#### **B. New Registration (Create Mutation)**
For a new teacher onboarding, the handler is more sophisticated, including field-level error mapping:
```javascript
addMutation.mutate(requestPayload, {
  onSuccess: (res) => {
    if (res.success) {
      // Redirects to the main teachers list page
      navigate('/admin/teachers');
    } else {
      // Handles specific "ValidationError" from the server
      const err = res.error;
      if (err?.type === 'ValidationError' && err.details?.fields) {
        const errorsMap = {};
        err.details.fields.forEach((item) => {
          errorsMap[item.field] = item.message;
        });
        setFieldErrors(errorsMap); // Updates UI to highlight specific fields
        setError(err.message || 'Please fix the errors highlighted below.');
      } else {
        // Fallback for general server errors
        setError(res.message || err?.message || 'Failed to register faculty.');
      }
    }
  },
  onError: (err) => setError(err.message)
});
```

### 2. Key Observations
*   **Navigation on Success:** Both branches use `react-router-dom`'s `navigate` to move away from the form once the operation is confirmed successful by the server (`res.success`).
*   **Standard Envelope:** The code expects an "envelope" response format where `success` is a boolean, and the actual error details are nested under `res.error`.
*   **Field-Level Validation:** The "New Registration" logic is better equipped for backend validation, as it maps `err.details.fields` to a `fieldErrors` state, which is then passed to `FormField` components to display inline red text.
*   **Consistency:** The page follows the project's **V2 Architecture** by using TanStack Query mutations (`useCreateTeacherMutation`, `useUpdateTeacherMutation`) rather than raw `fetch` or `axios` calls.

### 3. Potential Improvements (Architectural)
*   **Edit Mode Error Handling:** Currently, the Edit Mode `onSuccess` only handles a general error message. It could be updated to support the same `ValidationError` field mapping used in the Create branch for better consistency.
*   **Cache Invalidation:** The success handler relies on the mutation hooks to handle cache invalidation (likely via `onSuccess` in `useTeacherQueries.js`). If not, the list page might show stale data after navigation.

However, the component suffers from high complexity (600+ lines), inconsistent API payload mapping between \\\"Create\\\" and \\\"Update\\\" modes, and fragile data parsing logic. Update mode packs most fields into a `metadata` object, while Add mode uses a flat structure with nested `salary_config` and `userData`.\\n  - **Scenario**: When a new field (e.g., \\\"Secondary Mobile\\\") is added to the system, it must be added in two divergent logic paths, increasing the risk of \\\"Update\\\" forgetting the field or using a different key than \\\"Add\\\".\\n  - **Impact**: High maintenance overhead and high probability of data synchronization bugs.\\n  - **Fix**:\\n    ```javascript\\n    // Abstract payload generation into a separate utility or use a consistent schema\\n    const mapFormToPayload = (data, isEdit) => {\\n      // Shared logic...\\n      return isEdit ? transformToUpdate(data) : transformToCreate(data);\\n    };\\n    ```\\n\\n- **[Fragile Numeric Parsing]**\\n  - **Cause**: Uses `parseFloat(formData.base_salary) || 0` and `parseInt(formData.experience_years, 10) || 0` directly during submission.\\n  - **Scenario**: If a user enters a salary with formatting (e.g., \\\"5,000\\\"), `parseFloat` will return `5`, resulting in significant data corruption.\\n  - **Impact**: Financial data loss/errors.\\n  - **Fix**:\\n    ```javascript\\n    const cleanNumber = (val) => typeof val === 'string' ? val.replace(/[^0-9.]/g, '') : val;\\n    // ...\\n    base_salary: parseFloat(cleanNumber(formData.base_salary)) || 0\\n    ```\\n\\n- **[Unsafe \\\"Update\\\" Error Handling]**\\n  - **Cause**: The `updateMutation` `onSuccess` callback only handles `res.message` and doesn't account for the structured `ValidationError` format that `addMutation` handles.\\n  - **Scenario**: If the update fails due to a backend validation error (e.g., duplicate email), the user sees a generic message instead of field-level highlights.\\n  - **Impact**: Poor UX and difficulty for users to resolve input issues.\\n  - **Fix**: Synchronize error handling logic between both mutations to use the `setFieldErrors` mapping.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 🟡 Medium & 🟢 Low Priority Issues\\n\\n- **[Non-Secure Password Generation]** (Medium)\\n  - **Cause**: `generatePassword` uses `Math.random()`.\\n  - **Scenario**: Predictable passwords if an attacker can determine the seed.\\n  - **Fix**: Use `window.crypto.getRandomValues`.\\n\\n- **[Monolithic Component Structure]** (Medium)\\n  - **Cause**: All sections (Basic Info, Professional, Assignment, etc.) are in one file.\\n  - **Impact**: Difficult to test sections in isolation; high re-render cost for the entire form on every keystroke.\\n  - If the backend is rigid, create a \\\"Mapper\\\" layer to handle the transformation outside the component.\\n2. **Implement Formal Schema Validation**: Replace manual `validateForm` with a library like `Zod` or `Yup`. This would allow for centralized type safety and more robust number/phone/email validation.\\n3. **Decompose Sections**: Break the form into smaller functional components to improve maintainability and performance (using `React.memo` for static sections).\\n\\n---\\n*Generated by Gemini CLI `code-self-assessor` Skill*\"\n}"

## MODEL ✨

**Analyzing Generalist's Findings** I'm reviewing the detailed report from the generalist. The core issues identified, particularly the inconsistent API payload mapping between 'Add' and 'Update' modes and the fragile numeric parsing, are my current focus for resolution.The `generalist` agent has completed a deep analysis of `AddTeacher.jsx` using the `code-self-assessor` skill. The component received a **Robustness Score of 5.8/10 (Moderate)**.

### 📊 Code Self-Assessor Report: `AddTeacher.jsx`

#### 🟠 High Priority Issues (Critical for Reliability)

*   **Inconsistent API Payload Mapping**: 
    *   **Issue**: Divergent logic paths for "Add" vs "Update" modes in `handleSubmit`. Update mode packs fields into `metadata`, while Add mode uses a flat structure with nested objects (`salary_config`, `userData`).
    *   **Risk**: High probability of "Update" forgetting new fields added to the system or using different keys than "Add", leading to data drift.
    *   **Fix**: Abstract payload generation into a single mapper function or align the backend contracts.

*   **Fragile Numeric Parsing**:
    *   **Issue**: Uses `parseFloat(formData.base_salary)` directly. 
    *   **Risk**: If a user enters a formatted number (e.g., "5,000"), `parseFloat` returns `5`, causing significant financial data corruption.
    *   **Fix**: Implement a `cleanNumber` utility to strip non-numeric characters (except decimals) before parsing.

*   **Asymmetric Error Handling**:
    *   **Issue**: The `updateMutation` lacks the structured `ValidationError` mapping (field-level highlights) implemented in the `addMutation`.
    *   **Risk**: Users get generic error messages on profile updates instead of specific field highlights, leading to a poor UX.
    *   **Fix**: Synchronize the `onSuccess` logic to use `setFieldErrors` for both mutations.

#### 🟡 Medium & 🟢 Low Priority Issues

*   **Non-Secure Password Generation (Medium)**: `Math.random()` is used for password generation. It should be replaced with `window.crypto.getRandomValues` for cryptographic security.
*   **Monolithic Structure (Medium)**: The 600+ line file combines UI, state, and complex mapping logic. It is recommended to decompose the form into smaller, section-based sub-components.
*   **Hardcoded Progress Logic (Low)**: The progress indicators (e.g., "75%") are hardcoded and do not reflect actual form completion.

---

### Analysis of Save Button Success Handling
As requested earlier, here is the specific breakdown of the success response logic:

1.  **Create Flow**: Successfully redirects to `/admin/teachers` and includes robust field-level error mapping if the server returns a `ValidationError`.
2.  **Update Flow**: Successfully redirects to the teacher's profile (`/admin/teachers/${id}`) but **fails to map field-level errors**, providing only a generic error message if validation fails.

**Strategic Recommendation**: The immediate next step should be to unify the payload mapping and error handling to ensure consistency between the "Add" and "Update" operations.

How would you like to proceed? I can help implement any of these fixes or refactor the component into smaller sections.

## MODEL ✨

Based on my analysis of `useTeacherQueries.js`, the `addMutation` (implemented via the `useCreateTeacherMutation` hook) **does not manually set a new entry** in the cache using `setQueryData`. Instead, it uses a **refetch strategy**.

### How it works:
In `useTeacherQueries.js` (lines 115-126), the `onSuccess` handler is defined as:

```javascript
onSuccess: (response) => {
  if (response.success) {
    // This triggers a background refetch for ALL teacher-related queries
    queryClient.refetchQueries({ queryKey: queryKeys.teacher.all });
  }
}
```

### Key Implications:
1.  **No Manual Cache Injection**: It does not optimistically add the new teacher to the `teacher.list` cache or create a specific `teacher.detail(id)` entry immediately using the response data.
2.  **Automatic Synchronization**: By calling `queryClient.refetchQueries({ queryKey: queryKeys.teacher.all })`, it marks all teacher lists and details as "stale" and immediately triggers a network request to fetch the updated list from the server.
3.  **Visual Delay**: Because it relies on a refetch rather than a manual cache update (`setQueryData`), there might be a short delay where the list page still shows old data until the background refetch completes, unless the user navigates away (which `AddTeacher.jsx` does immediately).

### Summary for your analysis:
*   **Updates cached data?** Yes, but by re-fetching from the server, not by updating the local state with the mutation response.
*   **Sets new entry in cache key?** Indirectly. It clears/refetches the `all` keys, so when you navigate to the list or detail page, a fresh entry will be created from the new server data.

If the backend takes time to process the new entry, there is a small risk that the refetch might occur before the database is fully updated, though usually, the API response ensures the transaction is complete.

     alert(error.message || 'An error occurred during registration');\n      }\n    });\n  };\n\n  const renderStep = () => {\n    switch (currentStep) {\n      case 1:\n        return <ProfileStep formData={formData} setFormData={setFormData} onNext={nextStep} onCancel={() => navigate('/admin/students')} />;\n      case 2:\n        return <ProgramStep formData={formData} setFormData={setFormData} onNext={nextStep} onBack={prevStep} />;\n      case 3:\n        return <EnrollmentStep formData={formData} setFormData={setFormData} onNext={nextStep} onBack={prevStep} />;\n      case 4:\n        return <FinanceStep formData={formData} setFormData={setFormData} onNext={nextStep} onBack={prevStep} />;\n      case 5:\n        return <ActivationStep formData={formData} setFormData={setFormData} onFinish={handleFinish} onBack={prevStep} isPending={registerMutation.isPending} />;\n      default:\n        return null;\n    }\n  };\n\n  return (\n    <div className=\"max-w-5xl mx-auto space-y-8\">\n      {/* Progress Stepper */}\n      <div className=\"mb-10 w-full rounded-2xl bg-white dark:bg-slate-900/50 p-6 shadow-sm border border-primary/5\">\n        <div className=\"flex items-center justify-between mb-4\">\n          <span className=\"text-sm font-semibold uppercase tracking-wider text-primary\">Step {currentStep} of 5</span>\n          <span className=\"text-sm font-medium text-slate-500 dark:text-slate-400\">{(currentStep / 5 * 100)}% Complete</span>\n        </div>\n        <div className=\"h-2 w-full overflow-hidden rounded-full bg-primary/10\">\n          <div \n            className=\"h-full bg-primary transition-all duration-500\" \n            style={{ width: `${(currentStep / 5 * 100)}%` }}\n          ></div>\n        </div>\n        <div className=\"mt-6 grid grid-cols-5 gap-2\">\n          {['Profile', 'Program', 'Batch', 'Finance', 'Activate'].map((label, idx) => {\n            const stepNum = idx + 1;\n            const isActive = currentStep >= stepNum;\n            return (\n              <div key={label} className={`flex flex-col items-center gap-2 ${isActive ? '' : 'opacity-40'}`}>\n                <div className={`flex h-8 w-8 items-center justify-center rounded-full text-xs font-bold ${currentStep === stepNum ? 'bg-primary text-white ring-4 ring-primary/20' : isActive ? 'bg-primary text-white' : 'bg-slate-200 dark:bg-slate-700 text-slate-600 dark:text-slate-300'}`}>\n                  {stepNum}\n                </div>\n                <span className={`hidden md:block text-[10px] font-bold uppercase ${currentStep === stepNum ? 'text-primary' : 'text-slate-500'}`}>{label}</span>\n              </div>\n            );\n          })}\n        </div>\n      </div>\n\n      <main>\n        {renderStep()}\n      </main>\n    </div>\n  );\n};\n\nexport default StudentRegistrationWizard;\n"
```json
  },
  "id": "synth_ce6dd6a1-dc77-4844-a6dd-95bd3f7c12ba_1779214881839_0"
}
```

---

## MODEL ✨

Based on my analysis of `StudentRegistrationWizard.jsx`, its custom hook `useRegisterStudentMutation`, and the underlying `student.mockApi.js`, the student registration form sends a **flat JSON object** representing the aggregate state of the 5-step wizard.

Unlike the `AddTeacher` form, which maps data into nested objects (like `salary_config` and `userData`) before sending, the `StudentRegistrationWizard` sends the raw `formData` state directly. The "normalization" into database entities (Address, Enrollment, Finance) is currently handled on the **API/Mock layer**.

### JSON Structure (Payload)

When `handleFinish` is called, the following structure is sent to the mutation:

```json
{
  "fullName": "John Doe",
  "gender": "male",
  "date_of_birth": "2000-01-01",
  "motherName": "Jane Doe",
  "fatherName": "Richard Doe",
  "email": "john@example.com",
  "mobile": "9876543210",
  "address1": "123 Street Name",
  "address2": "Suite 400",
  "city": "Mumbai",
  "state": "Maharashtra",
  "pincode": "400001",
  "emergencyContactName": "Jane Doe",
  "emergencyContactRelationship": "Mother",
  "emergencyContactPhone": "9876543211",
  "highestQualification": "High School",
  "previousInstitution": "City Public School",
  "passingYear": "2022",
  "grade": "A+",
  "profilePhoto": null,

  "programType": "academic",
  "admissionType": "regular",
  "couponCode": "",
  "referralId": "",
  "entranceScore": "85",
  "applicableScholarship": 500,

  "batchId": "BTCH-001",
  "batchName": "Alpha Batch",
  "courseId": "CRS-001",
  "courseName": "Advanced Mathematics",

  "initialPaymentAmount": "5000",
  "paymentMethod": "cash",
  "paymentDate": "2023-10-27",
  "transactionRef": "TXN123456"
}
```

### Key Differences from `AddTeacher`:
1.  **Flat vs. Nested**: `AddTeacher` nests account info under `userData` and salary under `salary_config`. `AddStudent` (Wizard) sends everything at the top level.
2.  **Naming Convention**: `AddTeacher` uses database-aligned names (`full_name`, `mobile_number`). `AddStudent` uses camelCase UI-centric names (`fullName`, `motherName`, `mobile`) which are then mapped in the `student.mockApi.js` to database fields (e.g., `student_name`, `mother_name`).
3.  **Transaction Logic**: The `AddStudent` payload is treated as a "Transaction" because it simultaneously creates a Student, Address, Contact, Education record, Enrollment, and Fee Account.

This flat structure is eventually deconstructed by the `registerStudentTransaction` function in the API layer to populate multiple tables.

---

## MODEL ✨

The `StudentRegistrationWizard.jsx` is a well-structured multi-step form, but it has several points of friction that can be optimized to improve the user experience and data integrity.

### 🛡️ Analysis of the 5 Steps

#### 1. Profile Step
*   **Robustness**: Comprehensive coverage of personal, contact, emergency, and educational data.
*   **Weakness**: **Information Overload**. It’s a massive single page with 4 major sections. Users are likely to experience "form fatigue" before even reaching Step 2.
*   **Friction**: Manual entry for City/State/Pincode and no validation for mobile/email before moving to the next step.

#### 2. Program Step
*   **Robustness**: Good separation of Program Type and Admission Context. Clear visual feedback for radio selections.
*   **Weakness**: **Dead-end "Apply" button**. The "Apply" button for the coupon code is a UI shell with no logic, which can frustrate users if they have a valid code.
*   **Friction**: The "Entrance Exam" section is static; it doesn't dynamically calculate the scholarship based on the score in the UI.

#### 3. Batch Step
*   **Robustness**: Live search functionality for batches and clear "selected" state.
*   **Weakness**: **Dependency Blindness**. It allows selecting a batch that might not belong to the Program Type selected in Step 2.
*   **Friction**: If the list of batches is long, the user has to scroll significantly.

#### 4. Finance Step
*   **Robustness**: Excellent visual summary of the "Financial Contract" and installment schedule.
*   **Weakness**: **Non-Interactive**. Users cannot adjust the installment dates or amounts even if they have special permission.
*   **Friction**: The $12,000 base fee is hardcoded in the component instead of being derived from the selected batch/course.

#### 5. Activate Step
*   **Robustness**: Clear summary of the student and batch before final submission.
*   **Weakness**: **Premature Submission**. It allows "Complete & Activate" even if the `initialPaymentAmount` is 0 or missing, which might conflict with "Activation" logic.
*   **Friction**: The payment method selection is small and hidden at the bottom of a long column.

---

### 🚀 Optimization Strategy (Reducing Friction)

#### **Strategy A: Implement "Smart Defaults" & Automation**
*   **Pincode Lookup**: Integrate a small utility to auto-fill City/State when a 6-digit pincode is entered.
*   **Dynamic Fee Fetching**: In Step 4 (Finance), fetch the `baseFee` directly from the `selectedCourse` metadata instead of using a hardcoded $12,000.

#### **Strategy B: Progressive Disclosure & Validation**
*   **Inline Validation**: Don't wait for the "Save & Continue" button. Add red/green indicators for Email and Mobile as the user types.
*   **Step-Level Locks**: Disable the "Save & Continue" button if required fields (FullName, Mobile, ProgramType) are empty. Currently, a user can click "Next" on an empty form.

#### **Strategy C: UX UI Refinement**
*   **Decompose Profile Step**: Split "Step 1: Profile" into two sub-steps: *1a: Personal Info* and *1b: Education & Address*. This reduces the vertical scroll and makes the task feel "lighter."
*   **Auto-Scroll to Top**: Ensure that clicking "Next" scrolls the window to the top. Currently, if Step 1 is long, the user might land in the middle of Step 2.

#### **Strategy D: Batch Selection Filter**
*   **Contextual Filtering**: Automatically filter the batch list in Step 3 based on the `programType` and `admissionType` chosen in Step 2. This prevents users from making incompatible selections.

---

### 🛠️ Suggested Implementation: The "Quick Fix" for Step 4
To fix the hardcoded fee issue in `FinanceStep.jsx`, update the calculation logic:

```javascript
// Change this:
const baseFee = 12000; 

// To this:
const baseFee = useMemo(() => {
  return formData.courseFee || 12000; // Fallback to 12k if not set
}, [formData.courseFee]);
```

Would you like me to implement any of these specific optimizations (e.g., Pincode lookup or Batch filtering)?

ok what if we merge two steps `Program` and `Batch` in single step 2. and rename the step. think about ti.

## MODEL ✨

**Merging Steps** I'm working on consolidating the "Program" and "Batch" selections into a single "Enrollment" step within the `StudentRegistrationWizard.jsx` component. This should streamline the user experience from the current five steps down to four.Merging the **Program** and **Batch** steps into a single **"Academic Enrollment"** step is a brilliant move for reducing friction. Currently, Step 2 (Program) collects the "Intent" and Step 3 (Batch) handles the "Execution," but they are fundamentally two halves of the same decision.

Here is an analysis of why this merger works and how to structure it:

### 🎯 Why this Merges well
1.  **Immediate Filtering**: As soon as a user selects a "Program Type" (e.g., Single Course) or an "Admission Type," the Batch list can filter instantly on the same screen. This eliminates the "Back-and-Forth" if a user discovers their preferred batch isn't available for their chosen program.
2.  **Visual Momentum**: Reducing the wizard from 5 steps to 4 makes the process feel significantly faster. The progress bar jumps 25% with each step, which is psychologically more rewarding for the user.
3.  **Contextual Logic**: Benefits like Scholarships (Step 2) and Fees (Step 4) are both tied to the Batch (Step 3). Putting the Batch selection right after the Program/Benefit section keeps the mental model "Academic" before moving to "Financial."

### 🗺️ The New 4-Step Structure
1.  **Step 1: Student Profile** (Personal, Contact, Education)
2.  **Step 2: Academic Enrollment** (Program, Benefits, and Batch Selection)
3.  **Step 3: Financial Contract** (Review Installments & Discounts)
4.  **Step 4: Account Activation** (Initial Payment & Finalize)

---

### 🛠️ Proposed Layout for the Merged Step 2
To prevent the page from becoming too long, I suggest a **"Master-Detail"** or **"Top-Down"** layout:

*   **Top (Narrow)**: Program Selection & Admission Type (High-level choices).
*   **Middle (Cards)**: Apply Benefits (Coupon/Scholarship - collapsible if not needed).
*   **Bottom (Grid)**: Batch Selection (The result of the choices above).

### ⚠️ Challenges to Solve
*   **Vertical Scrolling**: Step 2 will now be quite tall. We should use the "Sticky Header" or "Auto-scroll to Batch" logic so when they pick a Program, the UI smoothly scrolls down to the available batches.
*   **Loading States**: Since Batch selection requires an API call (`useBatchesQuery`), we need a clean skeleton loader that covers only the batch section while the user is filling out the Program details.

### 📝 Updated Plan
I have updated the mental roadmap. If you approve, I can start by creating a new `AcademicEnrollmentStep.jsx` that combines the logic of `ProgramStep` and `EnrollmentStep`, and then update the `StudentRegistrationWizard.jsx` to reflect the 4-step flow.

Shall I proceed with creating the merged component?

ok now suppose that we want to merge these two steps in single page, and want to design the page layout in optimal way so that its vertical scrolling can be reduced using the compact design. now i will design this new design page using the stich so that write the prompt for google  stich agents.

## MODEL ✨

**Designing Academic Enrollment** I'm currently focused on consolidating "Program Selection" and "Batch Selection" into a singular, streamlined Step 2 within the `StudentRegistrationWizard.jsx`. My immediate next step is to craft a precise prompt for the "Google Stitch" agent to guide its UI generation for this integrated enrollment phase.**Optimizing Registration Workflow** I'm refining the layout for Step 2, focusing on an optimal, compact design to minimize vertical scrolling. This involves splitting configuration inputs like program type and admission details into a distinct column from the batch selection, utilizing card-based toggles, and dynamically revealing fields based on admission type. Additionally, I'm exploring a compact "Benefit" sidebar for coupon and referral codes.**Developing Enrollment Interface** My focus is on integrating program and batch selection into a singular, high-density UI for the registration wizard. I'm refining a two-column layout, ensuring programmatic selections dynamically filter batch options and maintaining a clean, modern aesthetic consistent with v2 primitives.This is a great strategic move. To achieve a compact, high-density design that fits both **Program Selection** and **Batch Selection** on a single screen (minimizing scroll), we should move from a "Top-to-Bottom" layout to a **"Split-Panel" or "Master-Detail" 2-column layout**.

Here is a professionally crafted prompt for the Google Stitch agent (or any AI UI design tool) to generate this specific view:

---

### 🎨 Prompt for UI Design Agent (Stitch)

**Task:** Design a high-density, 2-column "Academic Enrollment" step for an ERP Student Registration Wizard. The goal is to merge Program Configuration and Batch Selection into one screen while minimizing vertical scrolling.

**Layout Architecture:**
*   **Column 1 (Left - 35% Width): "Program Configuration"**
    *   Use **Segmented Controls** (pill-style toggles) instead of large radio buttons for *Program Type* (Academic Package vs. Single Course).
    *   **Conditional Inputs:** A compact dropdown for *Admission Type*. If "Entrance Exam" is selected, show a small, inline input for *Entrance Score* and a read-only *Scholarship %* badge.
    *   **Benefit Section:** A collapsed or low-profile area for *Coupon Code* and *Referral ID* using small, high-density text fields (height ~36px).

*   **Column 2 (Right - 65% Width): "Live Batch Selection"**
    *   **Header:** Integrated search bar with a "Results Count" indicator.
    *   **Selection Grid:** A vertically scrollable container for Batch Cards.
    *   **Batch Card Design (Compact):** Each card should be dense. 
        *   Top Row: Batch Name (Bold) + "Selected" Checkmark indicator.
        *   Middle Row: Course Name (Subtext).
        *   Bottom Row: Two small chips showing *[Icon] Teacher Name* and *[Icon] Schedule (e.g., M/W/F • 10AM)*.
    *   **Visual State:** Distinctive border and subtle background glow for the "Active/Selected" batch.

**Design Constraints:**
*   **Style:** Modern, clean, enterprise ERP aesthetic. 
*   **Palette:** Primary: Slate-900 (Text), Indigo-600 (Primary/Action), Slate-50 (Background).
*   **Density:** Tight padding (p-3 or p-4) and small font sizes (12px-14px) to ensure the majority of the content is visible "above the fold."
*   **Responsiveness:** On Mobile, the layout should stack vertically, but on Tablet/Desktop, it must remain side-by-side to reduce height.

**Interactive Logic to Visualize:**
*   Selection in Column 1 should visually "gray out" or update the availability of batches in Column 2.

---

### 💡 Why this design reduces friction:
1.  **Zero-Scroll Selection**: On a standard laptop screen, the user can see their program choices and pick a batch without scrolling at all.
2.  **Instant Feedback**: The user sees the impact of their "Entrance Score" on their "Scholarship" and how that relates to the "Available Batches" in one glance.
3.  **Logical Flow**: Left-to-Right processing is more natural for configuration-heavy tasks.

**Would you like me to start building the React structure for this 2-column component now?**

This component will adopt a **Split-Panel Layout**:\n- **Left Column (40% width):** Program Configuration (Program Type, Admission Type, Scholarship, Benefits).\n- **Right Column (60% width):** Live Batch Selection (Searchable, scrollable list of batches).\n\nThis design minimizes vertical scrolling and allows the user to see how their \"Program\" choices filter the \"Available Batches\" in real-time.\n\n## 2. Component Mapping (HTML to V2 UI Primitives)\n\nBased on the `components.md` memory and V2 Architecture used in `AddTeacher.jsx`, we will map the HTML elements to the following React components:\n\n### Left Column: Program Configuration\n| HTML Element/Section | Target V2 Component | Details |\n| :--- | :--- | :--- |\n| Program Selection Toggles | `SegmentedControl` | Replace the custom HTML buttons with `<SegmentedControl options={...} />`. |\n| Admission Type Dropdown | `SelectInput` | Wrap in `<FormField>` for consistent labeling. Options: Regular, Transfer, Entrance. |\n| Entrance Exam Score | `TextInput` | Type: `number`. Add an ad-hoc `%` suffix element or use a specialized input if available. |\n| Scholarship % (Read-only) | *Custom UI Div* | Use the HTML's `bg-primary/10` highlighted container to show real-time calculated %. |\n| Coupon & Referral ID | `TextInput` | Wrap in `<FormField>`. Include the \"Apply\" button beside the Coupon field. |\n\n### Right Column: Batch Selection\n| HTML Element/Section | Target V2 Component | Details |\n| :--- | :--- | :--- |\n| Batch Search Bar | `TextInput` | With left icon `search`. Binds to local `searchQuery` state. |\n| Batch Cards List | *Custom Grid* | Since batch cards have complex layouts (teacher image, schedule chips, active radio states), we will map the raw HTML into a reusable `BatchCard` local sub-component. |\n| Radio Selection | Standard `<input type=\"radio\">` | Managed by React state `formData.batchId`. The active state triggers the `border-primary` ring. |\n\n## 3. Data Flow & State Management\n\n### Props\nThe new component will receive the same props as other steps:\n```jsx\n{\n  formData: Object,\n  setFormData: Function,\n  onNext: Function,\n  onBack: Function\n}\n```\n\n### Local State\n- `searchQuery` (string): Filters the batch list.\n- `filteredBatches` (Array): Derived state filtering `batchesData` based on `searchQuery` and `formData.programType`.\n\n### External Data Integration (TanStack Query)\n- **Batches:** Use the existing `useBatchesQuery()` from `../../../batch/hooks/useBatchQueries`.\n\n### Dynamic Logic Implementation\n1.  **Entrance Score to Scholarship:** Create a `useMemo` block that calculates `formData.applicableScholarship` based on `formData.entranceScore`.\n2.  **Batch Filtering:** The right column will filter available batches based on the selected Program Type (e.g., if \"Single Course\" is selected, only show batches tagged as single subjects).\n\n## 4. Integration into Student Registration Wizard\n1.  **Update `StudentRegistrationWizard.jsx`:**\n    - Reduce the `currentStep` max from 5 to 4.\n    - Rename Step 2 in the progress stepper to \"Academic\".\n    - Replace the switch-case logic:\n      - `case 2: return <AcademicEnrollmentStep ... />`\n      - `case 3: return <FinanceStep ... />` (shift down)\n      - `case 4: return <ActivationStep ... />` (shift down)\n2.  **State Consolidation:** The `formData` object is already flat, so no major payload restructuring is needed for `student.mockApi.js`.\n\n## 5. Execution Steps\n1.  **Create File:** `src/features/student/registration/steps/AcademicEnrollmentStep.jsx`.\n2.  **Scaffold Layout:** Copy the Tailwind layout classes from `code_v2.html` (the 40/60 split).\n3.  **Implement Left Column:** Swap raw inputs for `SegmentedControl` and `TextInput`.\n4.  **Implement Right Column:** Integrate `useBatchesQuery` and map the data over the `BatchCard` HTML structure.\n5.  **Wire Orchestration:** Update `StudentRegistrationWizard.jsx` to render the new step and adjust the step counter.\n6.  **Cleanup:** Remove old `ProgramStep.jsx` and `EnrollmentStep.jsx` to maintain a clean codebase.",

```json
    "content": "# Plan: Convert V2 HTML to React Component (Academic Enrollment Step)\n\n**Target Component:** `src/features/student/registration/steps/AcademicEnrollmentStep.jsx`\n**Objective:** Merge Program and Batch selection into a single 2-column high-density interface, converting the raw `code_v2.html` design into a React component utilizing existing V2 UI primitives.\n\n## 1. Architectural Strategy\nWe will create a new step component `AcademicEnrollmentStep.jsx` to replace `ProgramStep.jsx` and `EnrollmentStep.jsx`. This component will adopt a **Split-Panel Layout**:\n- **Left Column (40% width):** Program Configuration (Program Type, Admission Type, Scholarship, Benefits).\n- **Right Column (60% width):** Live Batch Selection (Searchable, scrollable list of batches).\n\nThis design minimizes vertical scrolling and allows the user to see how their \"Program\" choices filter the \"Available Batches\" in real-time.\n\n## 2. Component Mapping (HTML to V2 UI Primitives)\n\nBased on the `components.md` memory and V2 Architecture used in `AddTeacher.jsx`, we will map the HTML elements to the following React components:\n\n### Left Column: Program Configuration\n| HTML Element/Section | Target V2 Component | Details |\n| :--- | :--- | :--- |\n| Program Selection Toggles | `SegmentedControl` | Replace the custom HTML buttons with `<SegmentedControl options={...} />`. |\n| Admission Type Dropdown | `SelectInput` | Wrap in `<FormField>` for consistent labeling. Options: Regular, Transfer, Entrance. |\n| Entrance Exam Score | `TextInput` | Type: `number`. Add an ad-hoc `%` suffix element or use a specialized input if available. |\n| Scholarship % (Read-only) | *Custom UI Div* | Use the HTML's `bg-primary/10` highlighted container to show real-time calculated %. |\n| Coupon & Referral ID | `TextInput` | Wrap in `<FormField>`. Include the \"Apply\" button beside the Coupon field. |\n\n### Right Column: Batch Selection\n| HTML Element/Section | Target V2 Component | Details |\n| :--- | :--- | :--- |\n| Batch Search Bar | `TextInput` | With left icon `search`. Binds to local `searchQuery` state. |\n| Batch Cards List | *Custom Grid* | Since batch cards have complex layouts (teacher image, schedule chips, active radio states), we will map the raw HTML into a reusable `BatchCard` local sub-component. |\n| Radio Selection | Standard `<input type=\"radio\">` | Managed by React state `formData.batchId`. The active state triggers the `border-primary` ring. |\n\n## 3. Data Flow & State Management\n\n### Props\nThe new component will receive the same props as other steps:\n```jsx\n{\n  formData: Object,\n  setFormData: Function,\n  onNext: Function,\n  onBack: Function\n}\n```\n\n### Local State\n- `searchQuery` (string): Filters the batch list.\n- `filteredBatches` (Array): Derived state filtering `batchesData` based on `searchQuery` and `formData.programType`.\n\n### External Data Integration (TanStack Query)\n- **Batches:** Use the existing `useBatchesQuery()` from `../../../batch/hooks/useBatchQueries`.\n\n### Dynamic Logic Implementation\n1.  **Entrance Score to Scholarship:** Create a `useMemo` block that calculates `formData.applicableScholarship` based on `formData.entranceScore`.\n2.  **Batch Filtering:** The right column will filter available batches based on the selected Program Type (e.g., if \"Single Course\" is selected, only show batches tagged as single subjects).\n\n## 4. Integration into Student Registration Wizard\n1.  **Update `StudentRegistrationWizard.jsx`:**\n    - Reduce the `currentStep` max from 5 to 4.\n    - Rename Step 2 in the progress stepper to \"Academic\".\n    - Replace the switch-case logic:\n      - `case 2: return <AcademicEnrollmentStep ... />`\n      - `case 3: return <FinanceStep ... />` (shift down)\n      - `case 4: return <ActivationStep ... />` (shift down)\n2.  **State Consolidation:** The `formData` object is already flat, so no major payload restructuring is needed for `student.mockApi.js`.\n\n## 5. Execution Steps\n1.  **Create File:** `src/features/student/registration/steps/AcademicEnrollmentStep.jsx`.\n2.  **Scaffold Layout:** Copy the Tailwind layout classes from `code_v2.html` (the 40/60 split).\n3.  **Implement Left Column:** Swap raw inputs for `SegmentedControl` and `TextInput`.\n4.  **Implement Right Column:** Integrate `useBatchesQuery` and map the data over the `BatchCard` HTML structure.\n5.  **Wire Orchestration:** Update `StudentRegistrationWizard.jsx` to render the new step and adjust the step counter.\n6.  **Cleanup:** Remove old `ProgramStep.jsx` and `EnrollmentStep.jsx` to maintain a clean codebase."
  },
```

## MODEL ✨

**Seeking User Agreement** I'm shifting my approach to confirm the execution plan directly with you, given recent file writing difficulties. This allows us to maintain progress while troubleshooting the underlying issue.**Confirming Plan for User** I'm focusing on obtaining your direct confirmation of the planned steps. This ensures we are aligned and can proceed efficiently, especially while we work through the file writing issues.I have successfully read the raw `code_v2.html` file and analyzed the existing V2 UI components from the project's memory.

Since we are merging the Program and Batch steps, this new "Academic Enrollment" step will utilize a powerful Split-Panel layout to prevent vertical scrolling.

Here is the robust implementation plan for converting the HTML to a React component and integrating it into the `StudentRegistrationWizard`:

### Plan: Convert V2 HTML to React Component (Academic Enrollment Step)

**Target Component:** `src/features/student/registration/steps/AcademicEnrollmentStep.jsx`
**Objective:** Merge Program and Batch selection into a single 2-column high-density interface, converting the raw `code_v2.html` design into a React component utilizing existing V2 UI primitives.

## 1. Architectural Strategy
We will create a new step component `AcademicEnrollmentStep.jsx` to replace `ProgramStep.jsx` and `EnrollmentStep.jsx`. This component will adopt a **Split-Panel Layout**:
- **Left Column (40% width):** Program Configuration (Program Type, Admission Type, Scholarship, Benefits).
- **Right Column (60% width):** Live Batch Selection (Searchable, scrollable list of batches).

This design minimizes vertical scrolling and allows the user to see how their "Program" choices filter the "Available Batches" in real-time.

## 2. Component Mapping (HTML to V2 UI Primitives)

Based on the `components.md` memory and V2 Architecture, we will map the HTML elements to the following React components:

### Left Column: Program Configuration
| HTML Element/Section | Target V2 Component | Details |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Program Selection Toggles | `SegmentedControl` | Replace the custom HTML buttons with `<SegmentedControl options={...} />`. |
| Admission Type Dropdown | `SelectInput` | Wrap in `<FormField>` for consistent labeling. Options: Regular, Transfer, Entrance. |
| Entrance Exam Score | `TextInput` | Type: `number`. Add an ad-hoc `%` suffix element or use a specialized input if available. |
| Scholarship % (Read-only) | *Custom UI Div* | Use the HTML's `bg-primary/10` highlighted container to show real-time calculated %. |
| Coupon & Referral ID | `TextInput` | Wrap in `<FormField>`. Include the "Apply" button beside the Coupon field. |

### Right Column: Batch Selection
| HTML Element/Section | Target V2 Component | Details |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Batch Search Bar | `TextInput` | With left icon `search`. Binds to local `searchQuery` state. |
| Batch Cards List | *Custom Grid* | Since batch cards have complex layouts (teacher image, schedule chips, active radio states), we will map the raw HTML into a reusable `BatchCard` local sub-component. |
| Radio Selection | Standard `<input type="radio">` | Managed by React state `formData.batchId`. The active state triggers the `border-primary` ring. |

## 3. Data Flow & State Management

### Props
The new component will receive the same props as other steps:
```jsx
{
  formData: Object,
  setFormData: Function,
  onNext: Function,
  onBack: Function
}
```

### Local State
- `searchQuery` (string): Filters the batch list.
- `filteredBatches` (Array): Derived state filtering `batchesData` based on `searchQuery` and `formData.programType`.

### External Data Integration (TanStack Query)
- **Batches:** Use the existing `useBatchesQuery()` from `../../../batch/hooks/useBatchQueries`.

### Dynamic Logic Implementation
1.  **Entrance Score to Scholarship:** Create a `useMemo` block that calculates `formData.applicableScholarship` based on `formData.entranceScore` in real-time.
2.  **Batch Filtering:** The right column will dynamically filter available batches based on the selected Program Type in the left column.

## 4. Integration into Student Registration Wizard
1.  **Update `StudentRegistrationWizard.jsx`:**
    - Reduce the `currentStep` max from 5 to 4.
    - Rename Step 2 in the progress stepper to "Academic".
    - Replace the switch-case logic:
      - `case 2: return <AcademicEnrollmentStep ... />`
      - `case 3: return <FinanceStep ... />` (was case 4)
      - `case 4: return <ActivationStep ... />` (was case 5)
2.  **State Consolidation:** The `formData` object is already flat, so no major payload restructuring is needed for `student.mockApi.js`.

## 5. Execution Steps
1.  **Create File:** `src/features/student/registration/steps/AcademicEnrollmentStep.jsx`.
2.  **Scaffold Layout:** Copy the Tailwind layout classes from `code_v2.html` (the 40/60 split).
3.  **Implement Left Column:** Swap raw HTML inputs for `SegmentedControl` and `TextInput` components.
4.  **Implement Right Column:** Integrate `useBatchesQuery` and map the live data over the `BatchCard` HTML structure.
5.  **Wire Orchestration:** Update `StudentRegistrationWizard.jsx` to render the new step and adjust the step counter.
6.  **Cleanup:** Remove old `ProgramStep.jsx` and `EnrollmentStep.jsx` to maintain a clean codebase.

## MODEL ✨

I have successfully implemented the merger of the **Program** and **Batch** steps into a single, high-density **Academic Enrollment** step.

### Key Changes:
1.  **New Merged Component**: Created `AcademicEnrollmentStep.jsx` which features a 2-column layout. The left column handles program configuration (Type, Admission, Scholarship, Benefits), while the right column provides a live, searchable batch selection grid.
2.  **Wizard Optimization**: Updated `StudentRegistrationWizard.jsx` to transition from a 5-step to a **4-step flow**. This significantly reduces user friction and provides a faster registration experience.
3.  **Real-time Logic**: Integrated automatic scholarship calculation based on entrance exam scores and dynamic batch filtering.
4.  **UI Consistency**: Utilized V2 UI primitives (`SegmentedControl`, `TextInput`, `SelectInput`) and adjusted navigation labels in the subsequent `Finance` and `Activation` steps to maintain a logical flow.
5.  **Codebase Cleanup**: Removed the deprecated `ProgramStep.jsx` and `EnrollmentStep.jsx` files to reduce technical debt.

The registration process is now more streamlined and visually aligned with the project's modern V2 architecture. How would you like to proceed?

}) => {\n      // Using generic query with limit 1 for details\n      const response = await apiClient.executeAction(\n        API_REGISTRY.DATA.QUERY, \n        { \n          target: 'Batch', \n item;\n        }\n      }\n      return undefined;\n    },\n    initialDataUpdatedAt: () => queryClient.getQueryState(queryKeys.batch.detail(id))?.dataUpdatedAt,\n    staleTime: 1000 * 60 * 5, \n  });\n};\n\nexport const useBatchStudentsQuery = (id) => {\n  const { token } = useAuth();\n  return useQuery({\n    queryKey: queryKeys.batch.student(id),\n    queryFn: async ({ signal }) => {\n });\n};\n\nexport const useBatchStudentsQuery = (id) => {\n  const { token } = useAuth();\n  return useQuery({\n    queryKey: queryKeys.batch.student(id),\n    queryFn: async ({ signal }) => {\n response.data?.data || [];\n    },\n    enabled: !!token && !!id,\n  });\n};\n\nexport const useWeeklyScheduleQuery = (batchId) => {\n  const { token } = useAuth();\n  return useQuery({\n    queryKey: queryKeys.batch.schedule(batchId),\n    queryFn: async ({ signal }) => {\n      const response = await apiClient.executeAction(\n        API_REGISTRY.BATCH.GET_WEEKLY_SCHEDULE, \n        { batchId }, \n        token,\n        { signal }\n      );\n      if (!response.success) throw new Error(response.message);\n      return response.data?.data || [];\n    },\n    enabled: !!token && !!batchId,\n  });\n};\n\nexport const useMasterTimetableQuery = (day) => {\n  const { token } = useAuth();\n  return useQuery({\n    queryKey: queryKeys.batch.master(day),\n    queryFn: async ({ signal }) => {\n      const response = await apiClient.executeAction(\n        API_REGISTRY.BATCH.GET_MASTER_TIMETABLE, \n        { day }, \n        token,\n        { signal }\n      );\n      if (!response.success) throw new Error(response.message);\n      return response.data?.data;\n    },\n    enabled: !!token && !!day,\n  });\n};\n\nexport const useCreateBatchMutation = () => {\n  const { token } = useAuth();\n  const queryClient = useQueryClient();\n\n  return useMutation({\n    mutationFn: ({ data, options }) => \n      apiClient.executeAction(API_REGISTRY.BATCH.CREATE, data, token, options),\n    onSuccess: (response) => {\n      if (response.success) {\n        queryClient.refetchQueries({ queryKey: queryKeys.batch.all });\n      }\n    }\n  });\n};\n\nexport const useUpdateBatchMutation = () => {\n  const { token } = useAuth();\n  const queryClient = useQueryClient();\n\n  return useMutation({\n    mutationFn: ({ id, data, options }) => \n      apiClient.executeAction(\n        API_REGISTRY.DATA.UPDATE, \n        { \n          target: 'Batch', \n          where: { batch_id: id }, \n          data \n        }, \n        token, \n        options\n      ),\n    onSuccess: (response, { id }) => {\n      if (response.success) {\n        queryClient.refetchQueries({ queryKey: queryKeys.batch.all });\n        queryClient.refetchQueries({ queryKey: queryKeys.batch.detail(id) });\n      }\n    }\n  });\n};\n\nexport const useBulkUpdateBatchesMutation = () => {\n  const { token } = useAuth();\n  const queryClient = useQueryClient();\n\n  return useMutation({\n    mutationFn: ({ ids, data, options }) => \n      apiClient.executeAction(\n        API_REGISTRY.BATCH.UPDATE_BULK, \n        { ids, ...data }, \n        token, \n        options\n      ),\n    onSuccess: (response) => {\n      if (response.success) {\n        queryClient.refetchQueries({ queryKey: queryKeys.batch.all });\n      }\n    }\n  });\n};\n\nexport const useDeleteBatchMutation = () => {\n  const { token } = useAuth();\n  const queryClient = useQueryClient();\n\n  return useMutation({\n    mutationFn: ({ id, options }) => \n      apiClient.executeAction(\n        API_REGISTRY.DATA.DELETE, \n        { \n          target: 'Batch', \n          where: { batch_id: id } \n        }, \n        token, \n        options\n      ),\n    onSuccess: (response) => {\n      if (response.success) {\n        queryClient.refetchQueries({ queryKey: queryKeys.batch.all });\n      }\n    }\n  });\n};\n."
```json
  },
  "id": "synth_ce6dd6a1-dc77-4844-a6dd-95bd3f7c12ba_1779261489164_12"
}
```

---

## MODEL ✨

I have updated the `useBatchesQuery` hook in `useBatchQueries.js` to implement a **Cache-First** local relation resolver strategy.

This update ensures that Step 2 of the student registration wizard will now instantly display batch data if it has been previously cached by *any* other list query in the application (e.g., from the main Batches management page), even if the specific filter key for the wizard hasn't been fetched yet.

### Implementation Details:
*   **`initialData`**: Added a fallback mechanism that searches through all existing `batch.list` queries in the TanStack Query cache.
*   **Performance**: If data is found in the cache, the `isLoading` state in `AcademicEnrollmentStep.jsx` will be `false` immediately, providing a zero-latency experience for the user.
*   **Stale Time**: Maintained `staleTime: Infinity` to prevent unnecessary background refetches once the data is loaded.

The registration wizard is now fully optimized to leverage the project's centralized cache. How would you like to proceed?

  onChange={(val) => handleChange('admissionType', val)}\n              options={[\n                { label: 'Regular Enrollment', value: 'direct' },\n                { label: 'Merit Based', value: </div>\n              </div>\n            </div>\n          </div>\n        )}\n\n        {/* Apply Benefits */}\n        <div className=\"bg-white dark:bg-slate-900/50 rounded-2xl p-6 shadow-sm ## MODEL ✨

I have successfully added a toggle bar to the "Apply Benefits" section in the `AcademicEnrollmentStep.jsx` component.

### Changes:
*   **Toggle Integration**: Introduced the `ToggleSwitch` component to control the visibility of the Benefits section.
*   **Smart Initialization**: The toggle state (`isBenefitsEnabled`) is automatically set to `true` if the student already has a coupon code or referral ID in the form data.
*   **Dynamic UI**: The Coupon and Referral fields are now conditionally rendered. When disabled, the section is compact, reducing vertical noise. When enabled, it reveals the inputs with a smooth entry animation.
*   **Visual Feedback**: Added a label to the toggle ("Enabled"/"Disabled") for clarity.

This refinement further reduces user friction by hiding optional configuration fields by default. How would you like to proceed?

---

## MODEL ✨

This is a smart optimization to handle peak hours or "walk-in" inquiries where you don't have time for the full 4-step wizard.

### 📋 Plan: Student "Quick Add" Mode

**Objective**: Create a high-speed, single-column form to capture essential data and "tag" a student to a batch for later completion.

#### 1. Minimal Data Points (Required Only)
To ensure maximum speed, we will only require:
- **Full Name**: Essential for identification.
- **Mobile Number**: Essential for follow-up.
- **Target Batch**: Essential to "attach" them to a group (per your note).
- *Optional Email*: Useful but not a blocker.

#### 2. UI/UX Strategy
- **Mode Toggle**: Add a "Quick Entry" vs "Full Wizard" toggle at the top of the `AddStudent.jsx` page.
- **Single-Column Layout**: A focused, narrow form (max-width: 500px) that can be filled in under 30 seconds.
- **Status Tagging**: Students added this way will be marked as `status: 'prospect'` or `'incomplete'`, so they stand out in the main list for later "finalization."

#### 3. Data Flow
- **Direct Mutation**: Bypasses the `registerStudentTransaction` logic and uses a simpler `quickRegisterStudent` function.
- **Batch Linking**: Creates a "Skeleton Enrollment" record with `status: 'draft'`, effectively reserving their spot in the batch without triggering fee installments.

---

### 🎨 Minimal Version (The "Quick Add" Form)

Here is how the compact UI will look:

```jsx
const QuickAddForm = () => {
  const [formData, setFormData] = useState({
    fullName: '',
    mobile: '',
    email: '',
    batchId: ''
  });

  return (
    <div className="max-w-xl mx-auto animate-in fade-in zoom-in-95 duration-500">
      <div className="bg-white dark:bg-slate-900/50 rounded-3xl p-8 shadow-xl border border-primary/10">
        <header className="mb-8">
          <h2 className="text-2xl font-black text-slate-900 dark:text-white">Quick Student Entry</h2>
          <p className="text-slate-500 text-sm mt-1">Capture basic lead info. Full registration can be completed later.</p>
        </header>

        <div className="space-y-6">
          <FormField label="Full Name" required icon="person">
            <TextInput 
              placeholder="e.g. Jonathan Smith" 
              value={formData.fullName}
              onChange={(e) => setFormData({...formData, fullName: e.target.value})}
            />
          </FormField>

          <FormField label="Mobile Number" required icon="call">
            <PhoneInput 
              placeholder="98765 43210"
              value={formData.mobile}
              onChange={(e) => setFormData({...formData, mobile: e.target.value})}
            />
          </FormField>

          <FormField label="Assign to Batch" required icon="groups">
            <SelectInput 
              placeholder="Search and select batch..."
              options={batchOptions}
              value={formData.batchId}
              onChange={(val) => setFormData({...formData, batchId: val})}
            />
          </FormField>

          <div className="pt-4">
            <button className="w-full bg-primary hover:bg-orange-600 text-white py-4 rounded-2xl font-black text-lg shadow-lg shadow-primary/20 transition-all active:scale-[0.98]">
              Register Prospect Student
            </button>
          </div>
        </div>
      </div>
    </div>
  );
}
```

### 🚀 Optimization Impact:
1.  **Friction**: Reduced by ~80% (from 30+ fields to 3).
2.  **Time-to-Save**: ~15 seconds.
3.  **Data Integrity**: We still capture the `batch_id`, which is your critical "anchor" for future work.

**Would you like me to implement this "Quick Mode" toggle in the `AddStudent.jsx` page now?**

Batch).\");\n      return;\n    }\n\n    // Payload for quick add\n    // Note: isRegistered: false and status: 'prospect' are usually handled by the backend/mock\n    const payload = {\n      userData: {\n        name: formData.fullName,\n        email: formData.email,\n        phone: formData.mobile\n      },\n      profileData: {\n        batch_id: formData.batchId,\n        referral_id: formData.referralId,\n        internal_notes: formData.notes,\n        status: 'prospect',\n        is_registered: false,\n        created_at: new Date().toISOString()\n      }\n    };\n\n    createMutation.mutate(payload, {\n      onSuccess: (res) => {\n        if (res.success) {\n          alert('Lead Registered Successfully!');\n          navigate('/admin/students');\n        } else {\n          setError(res.message || 'Failed to save student.');\n        }\n      }\n    });\n  };\n\n  return (\n    <div className=\"max-w-2xl mx-auto animate-in fade-in zoom-in-95 duration-500\">\n      <div className=\"bg-white dark:bg-slate-900/50 rounded-[2.5rem] p-10 shadow-2xl border border-primary/10\">\n        <header className=\"mb-10 text-center\">\n          <div className=\"inline-flex items-center justify-center w-16 h-16 rounded-2xl bg-primary/10 text-primary mb-4\">\n            <span className=\"material-symbols-outlined text-3xl\">bolt</span>\n          </div>\n          <h2 className=\"text-3xl font-black text-slate-900 dark:text-white tracking-tight\">Quick Student Lead</h2>\n          <p className=\"text-slate-500 text-sm mt-2 max-w-sm mx-auto\">\n            Instantly capture minimal details and anchor the student to a batch. \n            Full registration can be done later.\n          </p>\n        </header>\n\n        {error && (\n          <div className=\"mb-8 p-4 bg-red-50 dark:bg-red-900/20 border border-red-100 dark:border-red-800 rounded-xl text-red-600 text-sm font-bold flex items-center gap-3 animate-shake\">\n            <span className=\"material-symbols-outlined\">error</span>\n            {error}\n          </div>\n        )}\n\n        <form className=\"space-y-6\" onSubmit={handleSubmit}>\n          <div className=\"grid grid-cols-1 md:grid-cols-2 gap-6\">\n            <FormField label=\"Full Name\" required icon=\"person\" className=\"md:col-span-2\">\n              <TextInput \n                placeholder=\"e.g. Jonathan Smith\" \n                value={formData.fullName}\n                onChange={(e) => handleChange('fullName', e.target.value)}\n              />\n            </FormField>\n\n            <FormField label=\"Mobile Number\" required icon=\"call\">\n              <PhoneInput \n                placeholder=\"98765 43210\"\n                value={formData.mobile}\n                onChange={(e) => handleChange('mobile', e.target.value)}\n              />\n            </FormField>\n\n            <FormField label=\"Email Address (Optional)\" icon=\"mail\">\n              <TextInput \n                type=\"email\"\n                placeholder=\"jonathan@example.com\" \n                value={formData.email}\n                onChange={(e) => handleChange('email', e.target.value)}\n              />\n            </FormField>\n\n            <FormField label=\"Assign to Batch\" required icon=\"groups\" className=\"md:col-span-2\">\n              <SelectInput \n                placeholder={isBatchesLoading ? \"Loading batches...\" : \"Select target batch...\"}\n                options={batchOptions}\n                value={formData.batchId}\n                onChange={(val) => handleChange('batchId', val)}\n                disabled={isBatchesLoading}\n              />\n            </FormField>\n\n            <FormField label=\"Referral ID / Name\" icon=\"campaign\">\n              <TextInput \n                placeholder=\"Who referred this student?\" \n                value={formData.referralId}\n                onChange={(e) => handleChange('referralId', e.target.value)}\n              />\n            </FormField>\n\n            <div className=\"md:col-span-2\">\n              <FormField label=\"Internal Notes\" icon=\"notes\">\n                <textarea \n                  className=\"w-full rounded-xl border border-slate-200 dark:border-slate-700 bg-slate-50 dark:bg-slate-800 p-4 text-sm outline-none focus:ring-2 focus:ring-primary/20 focus:border-primary transition-all min-h-[100px] resize-none dark:text-white\"\n                  placeholder=\"Mention any specific requirements, source of inquiry, or follow-up notes...\"\n                  value={formData.notes}\n                  onChange={(e) => handleChange('notes', e.target.value)}\n                />\n              </FormField>\n            </div>\n          </div>\n\n          <div className=\"pt-6\">\n            <button \n              type=\"submit\"\n              disabled={createMutation.isPending}\n              className=\"w-full bg-primary hover:bg-orange-600 text-white py-4 rounded-2xl font-black text-lg shadow-lg shadow-primary/20 transition-all active:scale-[0.98] flex items-center justify-center gap-3 disabled:opacity-70\"\n            >\n              {createMutation.isPending ? (\n                <div className=\"w-6 h-6 border-4 border-white/30 border-t-white rounded-full animate-spin\"></div>\n              ) : (\n                <>\n                  <span className=\"material-symbols-outlined\">person_add</span>\n                  Register Lead\n                </>\n              )}\n            </button>\n            <p className=\"text-[10px] text-slate-400 text-center mt-4 uppercase font-bold tracking-widest\">\n              Automatic Fields: Created At, Status: Prospect, Registered: No\n            </p>\n          </div>\n        </form>\n      </div>\n    </div>\n  );\n};\n\nexport default QuickAddStudent;\n"
```json
  },
```
```json
  "id": "synth_ce6dd6a1-dc77-4844-a6dd-95bd3f7c12ba_1779265885023_22"
}
```
